Chapter 1 Introductory Material 1 
1.1 Foreword 2 
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 3 
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 4 
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-5 
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows:  6 
Release x.y.z 7 
where: 8 
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, ie, technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 9 
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 10 
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document.  11 
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating increment al changes during the 12 
editing process. 13 
1.2 Scope 14 
1.2.1  General  15 
The present document specifies the interoperability testing (IOT) for O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected 16 
using the O-RAN fronthaul (FH) interface. It is noted however that the same content can be utilized for the IOT for O-17 
DU and O-RU from the same vendor connected using the O-RAN FH interface. 18 
A guiding principle defining the tests in this document shall be that any test must exercise the fronthaul interface to a 19 
greater extent than the test prerequisite so that the test is a proper test of some fronthaul functionality or performance.  20 
All tests focus on testing the fronthaul interface, but due to the non-intrusive nature of the tests, system-level aspects of 21 
the O-DU and O-RU are inevitably part of the interoperability tests too.  Because of this, it is recognized that positive 22 
test outcomes indicate successful interoperability, but negative results may not be attributed solely to problems in the 23 
FH interface and additional investigation may be required. 24 
It is also noted that additional test scenarios are required for comprehensive testing of the  FH interface functionality and 25 
performance, which shall be considered in future WG4 test specification versions. 26 
In general, unless otherwise stated, the tests cover LTE (Stand-Alone), NR Non-Stand-Alone (NSA) and NR Stand-27 
Alone (SA). The tests shall be executed using whichever IOT profile(s) are appropriate for the DUTs. See Annex A for 28 
details on the IOT profiles. 29 
1.2.2  Summary of Test Scenarios 30 
The following set of interoperability test cases are defined for the current version of WG4 FH IOT specification. 31 
• FH tests focused on the M-Plane: 32 
o Start-up (O-RU start-up from the power-on of O-RU to the availability of service) 33 
• FH tests focused on the S-Plane: 34 
o Synchronization status detection 35 
o Frequency and time error (performance) 36 
• FH tests focused on the C/U-Planes: 37 
o Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment and Initial Radio U-Plane data transfer  38 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          6 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
o Radio downlink U-Plane data transfer (Downlink throughput performance) 1 
o Radio uplink U-Plane data transfer (Uplink throughput performance) 2 
• FH tests focused on the C/U-Plane Delay Management 3 
o Test with minimum, intermediate, maximum, and excess latency. 4 
1.2.3  Future Enhancements 5 
Additional test cases are under consideration for the future versions of this specification. A non-exhaustive list of 6 
candidate test cases for future versions is provided below: 7 
• FH tests focused on the M-Plane: 8 
o Software management (O-RU software update) 9 
o Fault management 10 
o File management 11 
• FH tests focused on the C/U-Plane: 12 
o Beamforming (testing the actual characteristics of the radiated/received signals at O-RU) 13 
o Compression (testing different compression methods and IQ bitwidth and validating expected 14 
performance) 15 
Note: beamforming and compression are tested as part of the IOT cases already specified in Chapter 2.2 16 
and the relevant IOT profiles (refer to Annex A for more details). The test cases above extend the 17 
capability to test the fronthaul interface in respect of these features. 18 
o Multiple O-RUs 19 
o Multiple UEs 20

1.4 Definitions and Abbreviations 30 
1.4.1 Definitions 31 
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1] and the following 32 
apply. A term defined in the present document takes precedence over the definition of the same term, if any, in 3GPP 33 
TR 21.905 [1]. 34 
C-Plane Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be 35 
confused with the UE’s control plane 36 
DL DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna 37 
eNB eNodeB (applies to LTE) <E-UTRAN NodeB / Evolved NodeB> 38 
fm-pm Fault Management, Performance Management role 39 
gNB gNodeB (applies to NR) <Next Generation NodeB> 40 
M-Plane Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-41 
RU 42

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.

NETCONF Network Configuration Protocol. For details see RFC 6241, “Network Configuration Protocol 1 
(NETCONF)”, IETF, June 2011 2 
NMS A Network Management System dedicated to O-RU operations 3 
NSA Non-Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of SgNB attached to MeNB 4 
O-CU O-RAN Central Unit – a logical node hosting PDCP, RRC, SDAP and other control functions  5 
O-DU O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower 6 
layer functional split. O-DU in addition hosts an M-Plane instance. 7 
O-RU O-RAN Radio Unit <O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF 8 
processing based on a lower layer functional split. This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but 9 
more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).>. O-RU in 10 
addition hosts M-Plane instance. 11 
PTP Precision Time Protocol (PTP) is a protocol for distributing precise time and frequency over 12 
packet networks. PTP is defined in the IEEE Standard 1588. 13 
PDCCH Physical Downlink Control Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface 14 
PBCH Physical Broadcast Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface 15 
SA Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of gNB attached to a 5G Core Network  16 
SCS OFDM Sub Carrier Spacing 17 
SSB Synchronization Signal Block, in 5G PBCH and synchronization signal are packaged as a single 18 
block 19 
sudo Super-User Do role 20 
subordinate The term “subordinate” is used as a replacement for “slave” and is consistent with its use in CUS 21 
specification. When consensus emerges on how to eliminate the use of the term “slave” in the 22 
referenced standards organization, that approach will be applied to this specification  23 
S-Plane Synchronization Plane: Data flow for synchronization and timing information between nodes 24 
SyncE Synchronous Ethernet, is an ITU-T standard for computer networking that facilitates distribution 25 
of clock signals over the Ethernet physical layer 26 
T-BC Telecom Boundary Clock 27 
TWAMP Two-Way Active Measurement Protocol 28 
UDP User Datagram Protocol 29 
UE User Equipment terminology for a mobile device in LTE and NR 30 
UL UpLink: data flow from the UE towards the core network, that is from the O -RU towards in the O-31 
DU in a Fronthaul context. 32 
U-Plane User Plane: refers to IQ sample data transferred between O-DU and O-RU 33

1.5 Introduction 1 
1.5.1 General 2 
O-RAN WG4 has specified and published the O-RAN FH interface specifications (CUS-Plane [2] and M-Plane [3]) 3 
with the objective to enable interoperability of O-DU and O-RU from different vendors. The aim of this document is to 4 
further facilitate such multi-vendor IOT using the O-RAN FH interface by defining standard test configurations, IOT 5 
profiles and interoperability test cases. 6 
It shall be possible to perform interoperability testing in a non-intrusive manner; that is, in a manner in which the 7 
network elements under test are not required to support any functionality or mode of operation beyond that required for 8 
normal operation in a telecommunication network. However, making the endpoints of the FH interface between the O-9 
DU and O-RU visible would require definition of new interfaces which may entail caching and transport of data. 10 
Furthermore, and more importantly, operators require that the total radio system function and perform adequately when 11 
integrating O-DU and O-RU from different vendors. Consequentially, this specification approaches interoperability 12 
testing by means of system level testing. 13 
FH interoperability testing by way of system test involves creation of a stimulus in the O-DU to O-RU direction using 14 
an actual or emulated O-CU, potentially with CN support/emulation, and measurement of the result at the output of the 15 
O-RU in the RF domain by an actual or emulated UE together with an RF signal/spectrum analyzer as required. 16 
Likewise, in the reverse direction, the stimulus to probe the FH in the O-RU to O-DU direction is provided by an actual 17 
or emulated UE and is measured at the output of the O-DU by an actual or emulated O-CU with CN support/emulation 18 
as required. 19 
Inasmuch as the interoperability testing by way of system test involves configuring and collecting results from the O -20 
RU it shall be effected by means of the M-Plane FH interface. For elements that fall outside of this scope, such as the 21 
O-DU, the configuration and collection of data and status information for testing purposes may be accomplished by 22 
NMS. 23 
Interoperability involves testing the FH interface in terms of M-Plane, S-Plane, C-Plane and U-Plane. Some aspects of 24 
these planes may be tested independently. However, some tests, such as those that require the devices to be brought into 25 
service and a call established entail simultaneous activity across multiple planes. 26 
1.5.2 Fronthaul M-Plane Architectural options 27 
As described in the “O-RAN WG4 Management Plane Specification” [3], two architectural models are supported, 28 
namely a “hierarchical” and a “hybrid” model. As a general guideline the following apply, 29 
1. Hierarchical model. The O-RU is entirely managed by one O-DU (sudo) using a NETCONF based M-Plane 30 
interface. 31 
2. Hybrid model:  The architecture allows one or more direct logical interface(s) between management system(s) 32 
(performing different roles, nms, fm-pm, swm, etc) and O-RU in addition to a logical interface between O-DU 33 
(sudo role) and the O-RU. 34 
1.5.3 Fronthaul Synchronization options  35 
Various synchronization options have been defined in the O-RAN WG4 CUS-Plane Specification [2] (LLS-C1, LLS-36 
C2, LLS-C3 and LLS-C4). Depending on the specific O-RAN deployment being considered, not all of them might be 37 
relevant. When testing the S-Plane, the System Integrator shall identify which of the test cases are relevant depending 38 
on the specific deployment scenarios addressed. As a general guideline the following applies:  39 
1. Direct connection between O-DU and O-RU:  40 
LLS-C1 is generally the main sync option to be validated  41 
LLS-C4 may be considered as an alternative or as a complement to LLS-C1 42 
2. Bridged network between O-DU and O-RU 43 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          11 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
LLS-C2 for cases where the synchronization is delivered to the O-RU via the O-DU and over the bridged 1 
network. In this case the PRTC/PRC may be embedded in the O-DU or may be located anywhere in the 2 
network (connected via backhaul or FH transport). 3 
LLS-C3 for cases when the synchronization is distributed to the O-RU without involving the O-DU In this case 4 
the PRTC/PRC may be located anywhere in the network (connected via backhaul or FH transport) and may 5 
also be co-located with the O-DU. 6 
LLS-C4 may be considered as alternative or as a complement to LLS-C2/LLS-C3. LLS-C4 is considered for 7 
future versions of the specification. 8 
The FH focused tests for S-Plane for the current version of this specification covers LLS-C1, LLS-C2 and LLS-C3 9 
using the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile (Full Timing Support). FH focused tests for S-Plane for LLS-C1, LLS-C2 and 10 
LLS-C3 using the ITU-T G.8275.2 [6] profile (Partial Timing Support), and LLS-C4 are for future study. 11

Chapter 2 Interoperability Measurements 1 
2.1  Interoperability Standard Test Definitions 2 
2.1.1  Standard Test Configurations 3 
Interoperability testing is performed to prove that the end-to-end functionality between the O-DU and O-RU is as 4 
required by the O-RAN FH CUS-Plane [2] and M-Plane [3] specifications on which these components are based. This 5 
requires system level testing with O-DU and O-RU as an integrated system. 6 
2.1.1.1  Device Under Test (DUT) 7 
The case where the O-DU and O-RU are provided by different vendors is the focus of this document, but the case where 8 
both are from the same vendor is also valid. 9 
The O-DU and O-RU, with their interconnecting FH, is considered as the DUT. This is the same whether the O-CU and 10 
O-DU are implemented as a combined node, or as stand-alone nodes.  11 
For simplicity and without prejudice the tests in the following sections are defined with reference to a stand-alone O-12 
DU. However, the tests apply equally when the O-DU is replaced by the O-DU functionality of a combined O-CU/O-13 
DU and where the Layer 2 and Layer 3 radio processing on the network side is provided by the O-CU functionality of 14 
the combined-node. Any differences to the test due to replacement of the stand-alone O-DU with a combined O-CU/O-15 
DU are detailed as they arise. 16 
The simplest test configuration involves a single O-DU and a single O-RU. In this configuration, the O-DU and O-RU 17 
are labelled as DUT1(O-DU) and DUT1(O-RU) respectively.  18 
More advanced test configurations will involve defining the cardinality between the 1 …M O-DU(s) and 1…N O-RU(s) 19 
as part of the test scenario which will determine the configuration required.  20 
An example of such test configuration is to have a single O-DU connected to multiple N O-RUs. In this example, the O-21 
DU is labelled as DUT1(O-DU) and the O-RU(s) are labelled as DUT1(O-RU) ... DUTN(O-RU) accordingly.  22 
A second example is to have multiple M O-DUs connected to multiple N O-RUs. In this second example, the O-DUs 23 
are labelled as DUT1(O-DU) … DUTM(O-DU) and the O-RU(s) are labelled as DUT1(O-RU) ... DUTN(O-RU) 24 
accordingly. However, deployment scenarios where a single O-RU is managed and used by more than one O-DU is not 25 
addressed in this version of the WG4 FH IOT Specification. 26 
External physical and or logical connection between the O-DUs and O-RUs are to be specified in the IOT profiles (eg. 27 
number of 10/25/40GE, physical medium eg. fiber), see Annex A for details. 28 
IOT test cases defined in the following sections of this specification shall be executed using whichever IOT profile(s) 29 
that are appropriate for the DUTs. See Annex A for more details on the IOT profiles.  30 
 31 
Figure 2-1: The simplest DUT configuration 32

2.1.1.2  Network Management System (NMS) 1 
Network Management System (NMS) is required to support M-Plane testing particularly in the Hybrid architecture 2 
model as the O-RU has logical connection with the NMS [3]. In the hierarchical model, the NMS manages the O-DU 3 
and the O-DU manages the O-RU respectively. 4 
External physical and or logical connection between the NMS and O-DUs and O-RUs are to be specified in the IOT 5 
profiles (eg. number of 10/25/40GE, physical medium eg. fiber), see Annex A for details.  6 
 7 
Figure 2-2: The relationship between DUT and NMS (hybrid mode connection to O-RU shown dashed) 8 
2.1.1.3  Testing Tools 9 
One of the key objectives of interoperability testing is to validate the functionality of production grade DUTs. Hence it 10 
is important to ensure that the DUTs are not negatively impacted with the utilization of internal functions solely to 11 
support interoperability testing. ie, DUTs are not expected to be testing tools when deployed in production networks and 12 
therefore DUTs should not be used as testing tools during interoperability tests.  13 
Interoperability tests are performed with a set of testing tools which are used to both apply active stimulus and as well 14 
as passive monitoring and measurements of the DUTs.  15 
The test is applicable to deployment scenarios where the O-CU and O-DU are implemented as separate nodes connected 16 
by an F1 interface and scenarios where they are implemented as a combined node without an accessible F1 interface. 17 
The deployment scenario where the 4G LTE eNB is implemented as separate 4G O-CU and 4G O-DU nodes connected 18 
by a W1 interface is considered for future versions of the WG4 FH IOT Specification when 3GPP standardization work 19 
for the W1 interface is complete.  20 
Active stimulus testing tools 21 
• 5G NR O-CU or O-CU emulator either as a separate node or as a combined node with O-DUs (DUT): 22 
used to provide Layer 2 and Layer 3 radio processing on the network side. In case of stand-alone nodes, 23 
terminates the 3GPP 5G F1 interface with the O-DU (DUT). 24 
o O-CU and O-CU emulator can be connected to either a real Core network or emulated Core. An 25 
emulated Core can be simpler to deploy for interoperability testing purposes. 26 
o External physical and or logical connection between the O-CU or O-CU emulator with the O-DU 27 
(DUT), if any, will be lab setup dependent either through physical or wireless medium 28 
• 4G LTE MeNB or MeNB emulator: used to terminate the 3GPP EN-DC X2 interface with the 5G NR 29 
O-CU or O-CU emulator  30 
o Required when the DUTs (O-DU and O-RU) are configured to operate 5G NR NSA option 3/3a/3x. 31

                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
o 4G LTE MeNB or MeNB emulator can either have physical or logical connection with the Test UE or 1 
UE emulator. RF connection between the 4G LTE MeNB or MeNB emulator with the Test UE or UE 2 
emulator will be either through cabled connection or Over the Air (OTA). 3 
• Test UEs and/or UEs emulator and optional beamforming network (for MIMO tests): used to 4 
generate stateful device connections and traffic to validate the O-DU and O-RU implementation of the O-5 
RAN FH interface protocols as these are stimulated by the 3GPP upper layer protocols.  The beamforming 6 
network (BFN), for example a Butler Matrix, is used to generate a static RF channel with rank not lower 7 
than the number of spatial streams required for the MIMO IOT test profile. 8 
o Required so that the O-RU which is the DUT does not need to be put into a “test mode” which does 9 
not happen in live deployments. 10 
o Test UEs will require SIM cards which are pre-provisioned with subscriber profiles. UEs used for 11 
testing can be simpler to setup but given that these Test UEs are designed to be commercial UEs with 12 
possibly certain diagnostic functions enabled for logging purposes, they are limited in terms of 13 
configurability. 14 
o UEs emulator will require SIM profile configuration with the subscriber’s profiles. UEs emulator can 15 
be used in test scenarios which require multiple UEs’ sessions, more flexibility and configurability to 16 
help drive test scenarios.  17 
o RF connection between the Test UEs or UEs emulator with the O-RU (DUT) will be either through 18 
cabled connection or OTA. However, in case BFN is used, the RF connection between the Test UEs 19 
or UEs emulator and the BFN is via cable and the RF connection between BFN and O -RU (DUT) is 20 
also via cable.  The use of OTA for MIMO tests is FFS. 21

Passive monitoring and measurements testing tools 26

preferred as span ports are less reliable but can be used if taps are not readily avai lable in the test lab. 24 
Connectivity specifics (eg. number of 10/25/40GE) are to be specified in the IOT profiles (see Annex 25 
A for details). 26 
• RF Spectrum and Beam Signal Analyzer: used for RF and Beam power and quality analysis for, 27 
o Test case validation and troubleshooting which can help with test setup validation and root cause 28 
analysis for test cases which fail 29 
Eg. the Beam Signal Analyzer can be used to validate that the O-RUs (DUT) are in-service, 30 
configured and operating correctly, which in case of 5G, includes validating that the SS/PBCH blocks 31 
(SSB) are configured with the correct Sub Carrier Spacing (SCS), transmitted at the correct frequency 32 
locations (can be offset from the center frequency), and in case of both 4G and 5G, burst periods with 33 
the correct Physical Cell Identities (PCI), Beam Identifiers and, expected power and quality. 34 
o RF Spectrum and Beam Signal Analyzer performs OTA RF measurements and signal analysis  35

2.1.1.4  Time Synchronization 3 
All the components including the DUTs (O-DUs and O-RUs) and the Testing Tools are required to be synchronized to a 4 
common system time and master time source unless otherwise stated. 5 
Synchronization Plane (S-Plane) configuration for the DUTs is specified in the IOT profiles (see Annex A for details).  6 
Test tools shall be time synchronized to the master timing source with PTP. 7 
2.1.1.5  Assumptions 8 
In this version of the WG4 FH IOT specifications, the following assumptions apply 9 
• All wireline transport interfaces and the air interface are assumed to conform to ideal conditions (no 10 
impairments). 11 
• All wireless connection assumed to adopt 3GPP approaches for “ideal” RF environment for test setup.  12 
• O-DU and O-RU comply to the same version of the O-RAN FH interface specifications. 13 
• All elements in the interoperability test and the supporting test environment, where 3GPP support is 14 
relevant, comply to the same version of the 3GPP Specification. 15 
• All O-RUs involved in a test are of the same category; all A or all B.  16 
2.1.1.6  Specifications to be used for testing 17 
In this version of the WG4 FH IOT specifications, the following sets of specifications and releases/versions shall be 18 
supported  19 
• O-RAN FH  20 
o Control, User and Synchronization Plane Specification [2] 21 
o Management Plane Specification [3] 22 
o Management Plane Yang Models [4] 23 
• eCPRI  24

2.1.1.7  Interoperability (IOT) Test Profiles 10 
The IOT Profiles are included in Annex A. Additional Profiles will be added in future releases of WG4 FH IOT 11 
Specification.  12 
2.1.1.8  Measurements of interest 13 
• Availability (eg. are the DUTs in service) 14 
• Accessibility (eg. can the device connect to the network) 15 
• Retainability (eg. can the device connection be maintained) 16 
• Mobility (eg. moving between two O-RUs) 17 
• Integrity (eg. data transfers between the device and the network) 18 
2.1.2  Standard Test Data Configurations 19 
The test data configurations are defined as part of the IOT profiles in Annex A.  20 
2.1.3  Standard Test Execution 21 
Most interoperability tests will follow a standard execution plan although individual test s are expected to deviate from 22 
this in some way. By defining the standard execution plan an understanding of how tests are arranged can be gained, 23 
thereafter examining individual tests can reveal how deviations from the standard execution plan may be defin ed.  24 
2.2  Interoperability Test Cases 25 
As stated in the introduction, interoperability involves testing the FH interface in terms of M -Plane, S-Plane, C-Plane 26 
and U-Plane. Some aspects of these planes may be tested independently. However, some tests, such as those that require 27 
the devices to be brought into service and a call established entail simultaneous activity across multiple planes  28 
Each interoperability test provides 1) test description and applicability, 2) the minimum requirements and prerequisites 29 
listing required testing tools as required, 3) test purpose and scope, 4) testability requirements imposed on the O -RU 30 
and O-DU, 5) test methodology with procedural description as required, 7) the test requirement and expected test result.  31 
Failure conditions are not addressed. 32 
The following set of IOT cases are defined in this document.   33 
M-Plane IOT Test  34 
1. Startup Installation: O-DU and O-RU getting in Service 35 
S-Plane IOT Tests  36

                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
1. Functional test of O-DU + O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1) 1 
2. Functional test of O-DU + bridged network + O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C2)  2 
3. Functional test of O-DU + bridged network + O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C3) 3 
4. Performance test of O-DU + Two O-RUs using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1) 4 
5. Performance test of O-DU + bridged network + Two O-RUs using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C2) 5 
6. Performance test of O-DU + bridged network + Two O-RUs using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C3) 6 
C/U-Plane IOT Tests 7

2.2.1  M-Plane IOT Test  16 
The M-Plane IOT test for hierarchical mode is described in Section 2.2.1.1 and the respective test for hybrid mode is 17 
described in Section 2.2.1.2. Separate IOT profiles are defined for each mode. In this version of the specification NMS 18 
operation in hybrid mode is limited to read-only operation. 19 
2.2.1.1  Start-up in hierarchical mode 20 
2.2.1.1.1  Test Description and Applicability 21 
This scenario is MANDATORY. 22 
The DUT is composed of single O-DU and single O-RU. 23 
Test scenario refers to Chapter 3 “Start-up” in hierarchical architecture for M-Plane [3]. 24 
2.2.1.1.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 25 
Single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)) and a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU))  26 
• Must be connected through the O-RAN FH  27 
Assumptions which are required for this test scenario 28 
1. DHCP server is configured for test purposes (either function served by O-DU or external DHCP server with O-29 
DU or router as relay – that should have no impact on test scenario). In case of external DHCP server - 30 
Configuration of DHCP server and DHCP procedures are excluded from validation of IOT. 31 
2. As IPv6 support is optional, only IPv4 transport connection for M-Plane is used in this test. 32 
3. A combination of VLAN identity and MAC address is only used for C/U - Plane connectivity.  33 
4. Network between O-DU and O-RU allows for connectivity between actors. 34 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          19 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
5. O-RU has account configured with sudo access privilege. O-DU knows credentials of sudo account available 1 
at O-RU. 2 
6. Appropriate software file for O-RU is pre-installed in O-RU and corresponding manifest.xml is located in O-3 
DU. No software upgrade is required during startup test sequence of O -RU for this IOT test case. 4 
Testing tools which are required for this test scenario 5 
1. FH Protocol Analyzer monitoring traffic between O-DU and O-RU is used for validation of M-Plane 6 
procedural flows and contents of messages prior to the establishment of the SSH connection for M-Plane and 7 
when certain procedures do not use encryption (eg., loopback messages and responses of IEEE 802.1Q). 8 
2.2.1.1.3  Test Purpose and Scope 9 
Purpose of this test is to validate the startup sequence of O-RU and the interface to DHCP server and NETCONF client 10 
in O-DU for the start-up scenario. 11 
The detailed steps outlined in this test case are for informational purposes and can be useful for troubleshooting 12 
purposes in the event that the test case fails. Procedures which are not encrypted with SSH can be observed with the FH 13 
Protocol Analyzer for validation of the test progress. 14 
Notwithstanding this being an M-Plane test, correct evaluation of the success of the M-Plane operation requires also 15 
that the fronthaul C-Plane and U-Plane also be operational, at least in the DL direction. 16 
2.2.1.1.4  Testability requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU 17 
The appropriate software runs on the O-RU and O-DU for the test purpose. 18 
2.2.1.1.5  Methodology and Initial Conditions 19 
1. There is physical connectivity between O-RU and O-DU 20 
2. O-DU is powered up and in service or running 21 
3. DHCP server is connected and available 22 
4. O-RU is powered up for this start-up test scenario 23 
5. The credential information (default username and password) is commonly pre -installed in O-DU and O-RU as 24 
one of test assumptions in 2.2.1.1.2. 25 
2.2.1.1.6  Procedure: M-Plane start up test 26 
2.2.1.1.6.1  Step: Transport layer initialization  27 
1. Depending on initial condition – either power-on to O-RU or physical network connection is enabled between 28 
O-RU and O-DU.  29 
2. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: DHCP Discovery coming from O-RU’s MAC address 30 
Note: message is sent as part of VLAN scan procedure, hence it can be in serial sequence “VID after VID with 31 
timer in between” or in parallel sequence “burst to subset of VIDs, timer, another burst to different subs et of 32 
VIDs”. FH Protocol Analyzer confirms that the O-RU includes vendor class (option 60) or vendor-identifying 33 
vendor class (option 124) in the DHCP DISCOVER. 34 
3. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: VLAN scan continues until response from DHCP server is received.  35 
4. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: O-RU continues DHCP procedure using only the VID on which response 36 
from DHCP server has been received. 37 
5. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: DHCP procedure is finished by DHCP Acknowledgement message sent 38 
towards O-RU. As a result of DHCP procedure, O-RU obtains its own IP details plus IP (option 43) or FDQN 39 
of corresponding NETCONF Client in O-DU. 40 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          20 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
2.2.1.1.6.2  Step: RU calls home to NETCONF client (TCP connection establishment) 1 
1. FH Protocol Analyzer observes Call Home – a TCP session establishment initiated by O-RU towards O-DU 2 
2.2.1.1.6.3  Step: SSH Secure connection establishment  3 
1. SSH session establishment initiated by O-DU towards O-RU. 4 
2.2.1.1.6.4  Step: NETCONF Capability discovery 5 
1. NETCONF Hello message sent by O-RU towards O-DU. The message exposes capability of ietf-yang-library 6 
2. NETCONF Hello message sent by O-DU towards O-RU 7 
3. <rpc><get> message sent by O-DU to O-RU. The <rpc><get> has <modules-state xlsnm = 8 
“urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-yang-library”> subtree filter imposed 9 
4. <rpc><reply> message sent by O-RU to O-DU. The message contains content of leaf “modules-state” of ietf-10 
yang-library.yang module 11 
2.2.1.1.6.5  Step: Optional provisioning of new management accounts 12 
Note: this step is intentionally omitted as pre-provisioned O-RU is expected for IOT (meaning: no need to perform 13 
optional step and configure supplementary management accounts). 14 
2.2.1.1.6.6  Step: Initial process of NETCONF Subscribe for each stream 15 
1. NETCONF “create-subscription” RPC message(s) sent by O-DU towards O-RU. Number of NETCONF 16 
subscriptions is up to O-DU.  17 
Note: O-DU can subscribe itself to default event stream or to specific streams of events. In case no subscription 18 
to default stream is performed, then O-DU shall subscribe itself at least to event streams “supervision-19 
notification” and “alarm-notif”. Subscription to other streams is optional, however not prohibited. 20 
2. NETCONF “create-subscription” RPC Reply messages sent by O-RU for each RPC message 21 
2.2.1.1.6.7  Step: Supervision of NETCONF connection 22 
1. Periodic sequence of NETCONF messages: 23 
a. supervision-notification sent by O-RU towards O-DU 24 
b. RPC supervision-watchdog-reset sent by O-DU towards O-RU 25 
c. RPC reply sent by O-RU towards O-DU 26 
Note: in above sequence following timers shall be respected: “supervision-notification-interval”, “guard-timer-27 
overhead” sent as parameters in RPC supervision-watchdog-reset (O-DU -> O-RU) and “next-update-at” sent as 28 
parameter in RPC reply (O-RU -> O-DU). 29 
2.2.1.1.6.8  Step: Retrieval of O-RU information and Additional configuration 30 
1. O-DU sends <rpc><get><filter=”subtree”> to get each yang module listed in ietf -yang-library.yang in O-RU, 31 
for example  32 
o ietf-hardware augmented by o-ran-hardware 33 
o ietf-interface augmented by o-ran-interfaces 34 
o o-ran-operations 35 
o o-ran-transceiver 36 
o o-ran-sync 37

1. O-DU sends <rpc><get><filter=”subtree”> to get o-ran-software-management.yang 19

1. O-DU configures by <rpc><edit-config> vlan-id for the usage of C/U-Plane in ietf-interface augmented by o-25 
ran-interfaces to O-RU. O-RU responds with <rpc-reply><ok/> 26 
2. O-DU sends loopback message to O-RU with MAC address and vlan-id periodically. The O-RU MAC address 27 
and vlan-id used in LBM is same as the one that set in ietf-interface augmented by o-ran-interfaces. 28 
3. O-RU sends loopback response to O-DU per received loopback message respectively 29 
2.2.1.1.6.11  Step: U-Plane configuration between O-DU and O-RU 30 
1. O-DU sends <rpc><get><user-plane-configuration> to determine the presence of following instances: multiple 31 
static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoints, multiple [tr]x-arrays and the relations between them. O-RU replies <rpc-32 
reply><data> including key information on number of endpoints, band number, number of arrays and 33 
polarization. 34 
2. O-DU sends <rpc><edit-config> to create low-level-[tr]x-endpoints, with the same name as static-low-level-35 
[tr]x-endpoints. The NETCONF Client is responsible for assigning unique values to the "eaxc-id" addresses of 36 
all low-level-rx-endpoint elements and low-level-tx-endpoint elements, within the O-RU when operating in the 37 
same direction (Tx or Rx), even when these operate across different named interfaces of the O -RU. Number of 38 
instances of low-level-[tr]x-endpoints depend on contents of selected test profile eg. for number of CCs. It may 39 
be less than number of instances of static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoints. O-RU replies <rpc-reply><ok/></rpc-40 
reply>. 41

                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
3. O-DU sends <rpc><edit-config> to create [tr]x-array-carriers. Number of created instances of [tr]x-array-1 
carriers is equivalent to number of CCs times number of arrays, where number of CCs is defined by operator. 2 
Appropriate values are configured to absolute-frequency-center, channel-bandwidth, gain, and so on. In 3 
provided configuration the value of leaf “active” is set as ‘INACTIVE’ (or leaf is omitted in configuration and 4 
O-RU uses its default value 'INACTIVE') for all just created [tr]x-array-carriers. O-RU replies <rpc-5 
reply><ok/></rpc-reply>. 6 
4. O-DU sends <rpc><edit-config> to create processing-elements related to interfaces offering access to desired 7 
endpoints. The key information such as MAC address is configured according to selected transport flow, eg. o-8 
ru-mac-address, o-du-mac-address and vlan-id for C/U-Plane in case of Ethernet flow. O-RU replies <rpc-9 
reply><ok/></rpc-reply>. 10 
5. O-DU sends <rpc><edit-config> to create low-level-[tr]x-link(s) to make relationship between low-level-[tr]x-11 
endpoint(s), [tr]x-array-carriers and processing elements belonging to transport. The number of instance(s) for 12 
low-level-[tr]x-links is equivalent to that of instance(s) of low-level-[tr]x-endpoints. 13 
2.2.1.1.6.12  Step: Fault Management activation 14 
1. O-DU sends <rpc><get><filter=”subtree”> to get o-ran-fm.yang 15 
2. O-RU responds with <rpc-reply><data> for <active-alarm-list><active-alarms> 16 
Note: subscription to NETCONF default event stream fulfils the condition to signal notification alarm-notif 17 
when O-RU detects any alarm. 18 
2.2.1.1.6.13  Step: Performance measurement activation (if required at start-up timing) 19 
Note: Step for Retrieval of O-RU information may cover the configuration of o-ran-performance-management.yang if it 20 
is required at start-up installation timing. 21 
2.2.1.1.6.14  Step: Retrieval of O-RU state, including synchronization information, from O-RU 22 
If O-DU already knows at the moment this step is going to be performed (e.g. from notification “synchronization -state-23 
change”), that “sync-state” of O-RU is ‘LOCKED’, O-DU may skip this step. 24 
S-Plane has to be operational. 25 
1. O-DU sends <rpc><get><sync> to O-RU 26 
2. S-Plane in O-RU has been locked, sends <rpc-reply><data> <sync-status><sync-state> LOCKED 27 
2.2.1.1.6.15  Step: Configuring the O-RU operational parameters: carrier activation 28 
S-Plane has to be operational (sync-state != FREERUN, preferable sync-state = LOCKED) prior to running this step 29 
1. O-DU sends <rpc><edit-config> to perform activation by setting the value of the parameter “active” at [tr]x -30 
array-carriers to “ACTIVE”. O-RU sends <rpc-reply><ok/> 31 
2. O-RU sends notification [tr]x-array-carriers-state-change that indicates all [tr]x-array-carriers’ names with 32 
“state” = “READY” 33 
Note: C/U-Plane service is available at this step. 34 
2.2.1.1.7  Test Requirement (expected result)  35 
Observe that both the O-DU and O-RU get in service successfully by monitoring correct transmission of 36 
synchronization signals and broadcast channel (ie, PSS/SSS and PBCH for LTE and SSB for NR).  37 
Record downlink carrier frequency (EARFCN for LTE as defined in 3GPP TS 36.104 [12] and GSCN/NR-ARFCN for 38 
NR as defined in 3GPP TS 38.104 [13]), cell (PCI for LTE and for NR as defined in 3GPP TS 36.211 [14] and TS 39 
38.211 [15], respectively) and system information (MIB for LTE and NR as specified in 3GPP TS 36.331 [16] and TS 40 
38.331 [17], respectively). In case that beam sweeping is applied to SSB, system information should be recorded for 41 
each of the SSB indices detected. 42

2.2.1.2  Start-up in hybrid mode 7 
2.2.1.2.1  Test Description and Applicability 8 
This scenario is MANDATORY.  9 
The DUT is composed of single O-DU, a single O-RU and a single NMS. 10 
Test scenario refers to Chapter 2 “M-Plane Architectural Model” and Chapter 3 “Start-up” in hybrid architecture for M-11 
Plane [3]. As per M-Plane Chapter 2, all compliant O-RUs shall be able to support both hierarchical and hybrid 12 
deployment. The testing of hybrid use case shall therefore include being able to demonstrate that an O -RU is able to 13 
support simultaneous NETCONF sessions to the O-DU and NMS. In order to ensure limited impacts to the baseline 14 
hierarchical O-DU to NMS configuration management tasks, in this test the second NETCONF client associated with 15 
“nms” user privileges is limited to demonstrating that it is able to retrieve the configuration and operational state from 16 
an O-RU which has been configured by an O-DU. 17 
2.2.1.2.2  Minimum Requirements 18 
Single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)), a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU)) and a single NMS (DUT1(NMS). 19 
Must be connected through the O-RAN FH  20 
Assumptions which are required for this test scenario 21 
1. DHCP server is configured for test purposes (either function served by O -DU or external DHCP server with O-22 
DU or router as relay – that should have no impact on test scenario). In case of external DHCP server - 23 
Configuration of DHCP server and DHCP procedures are excluded from validation of IOT.  24 
2. As IPv6 support is optional, only IPv4 transport connection for M-Plane is used in this test. 25 
3. A combination of VLAN identity and MAC address is used for C/U - Plane connectivity. 26 
4. A common VLAN is used for M-Plane connectivity between the O-RU and O-DU and between the O-RU and 27 
the NMS. 28 
5. Network between O-DU and O-RU and between NMS and O-RU allows for connectivity between actors.  29 
6. An account user-name has been configured for group “nms” access control privileges in a previous O-DU/O-30 
RU testing step as defined in sub-section 2.2.1.1.6.5. 31 
7. O-RU has two accounts configured. One account has sudo access privilege with credentials used by the O -DU. 32 
The other account has nms access privilege and the credentials used by the NMS. 33 
8. Appropriate software file for O-RU is pre-installed in O-RU and corresponding manifest.xml is located in O-34 
DU. No software upgrade is required during startup test sequence of O-RU for this IOT test case. 35 
9. An NMS is configured for supporting NETCONF Call Home functionality. 36 
Testing tools which are required for this test scenario 37 
1. FH Protocol Analyzer monitoring traffic between O-DU and O-RU and between NMS and O-RU is used for 38 
validation of M-Plane procedural flows and contents of messages prior to the establishment of the SSH 39 
connection for M-Plane and when certain procedures do not use encryption (eg., loopback messages and 40 
responses of IEEE 802.1Q). 41

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          24 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
2.2.1.2.3  Test Purpose 1 
Purpose of this test is to validate the startup sequence of O-RU and the interface to DHCP server and NETCONF clients 2 
in the O-DU and NMS for the start-up scenario. As described in [3], all O-RUs supporting the M-Plane specification 3 
shall support multiple NETCONF sessions, and hence all compliant O-RUs shall be able to support both hierarchical 4 
and hybrid deployment. 5 
The detailed steps outlined in this test case are for informational purposes and can be useful for troubleshooting 6 
purposes in the event that the test case fails. Procedures which are not encrypt ed with SSH can be observed with the FH 7 
Protocol Analyzer for validation of the test progress. 8 
Notwithstanding this being an M-Plane test, correct evaluation of the success of the M-Plane operation requires also 9 
that the fronthaul C-Plane and U-Plane also be operational, at least in the DL direction. 10 
2.2.1.2.4  Testability requirements imposed on O-RU, O-DU and NMS 11 
The appropriate software runs on the O-RU, O-DU and NMS for the test purpose. 12 
2.2.1.2.5  Initial Conditions 13 
1. There is physical and or logical  connectivity between O-RU and O-DU and between the O-RU and NMS 14 
2. O-DU and NMS are powered up and in service or running 15 
3. DHCP server is connected and available 16 
4. O-RU is powered up for this start-up test scenario 17 
5. The credential information (sudo username and password together with nms username and password) is 18 
configured on the O-RU according to one of test assumptions listed in in 2.2.1.2.2. 19 
2.2.1.2.6  Procedure: M-Plane start up test 20 
2.2.1.2.6.1  Step: Transport layer initialization  21 
1. Depending on initial condition – either power-on to O-RU or physical or logical network connection is enabled 22 
between O-RU and O-DU/NMS.  23 
2. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: DHCP Discovery coming from O-RU’s MAC address 24 
3. Note: message is sent as part of VLAN scan procedure, hence it can be in serial sequence “VID after VID with 25 
timer in between” or in parallel sequence “burst to subset of VIDs, timer, another burst to different subset of 26 
VIDs”. FH Protocol Analyzer confirms that the O-RU includes vendor class (option 60) or vendor-identifying 27 
vendor class (option 124) in the DHCP DISCOVER. 28 
4. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: VLAN scan continues until response from DHCP server is received.  29 
5. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: O-RU continues DHCP procedure using only the VID on which response 30 
from DHCP server has been received. 31 
6. FH Protocol Analyzer observation: DHCP procedure is finished by DHCP Acknowledgement message sent 32 
towards O-RU. As a result of DHCP procedure, O-RU obtains its own IP details plus an DHCP option 43 33 
carrying either IP or FDQN of corresponding NETCONF Clients in O-DU and in NMS. 34 
2.2.1.2.6.2  Step: RU calls home to discovered NETCONF client (TCP connection establishment)  35 
1. FH Protocol Analyzer observes Call Home – a TCP session establishment initiated by O-RU towards O-DU 36 
2. FH Protocol Analyzer observes Call Home – a TCP session establishment initiated by O-RU towards NMS 37 
2.2.1.2.6.3  Step: SSH Secure connection establishment  38 
1. SSH session establishment initiated by O-DU towards O-RU using sudo account privilege. 39

2. SSH session establishment initiated by NMS towards O-RU using nms account privilege. 1 
2.2.1.2.6.4  Step: NETCONF Capability discovery 2

of leaf “modules-state” of ietf-yang-library.yang module 9

optional step and configure supplementary management accounts). 12

1. NETCONF “create-subscription” RPC message(s) sent by O-DU towards O-RU. Number of NETCONF 14 
subscriptions is up to O-DU.  15 
Note: O-DU can subscribe itself to default event stream or to specific streams of events. In case no subscription 16 
to default stream is performed, then O-DU shall subscribe itself at least to event streams “supervision-17 
notification” and “alarm-notif”. Subscription to other streams is optional, however not prohibited. 18 
2. NETCONF “create-subscription” RPC Reply messages sent by O-RU for each RPC message 19 
Note: subsequent steps use the NMS to retrieve the configuration and operational state of the O-RU and are performed 20 
after step 2.2.1.1.6.7 through 2.2.1.1.6.15 that complete O-RU start-up. 21

2. O-RU responds with <rpc-reply><data> for each yang module per <rpc><get> 1 
2.2.1.2.8  Test Requirement (expected result)  2 
Observe that the O-RU calls home to both the O-DU and NMS and then is able to establish simultaneous NETCONF 3 
sessions between the O-RU and O-DU and between the O-RU and NMS. 4 
Observe that the NMS is able to retrieve configuration and operational state from models to which it does have NACM 5 
read privileges. 6

If the test case fails, vendor specific methods will be relied on to assist with troubleshooting the root cause(s) which led 8 
to the failure. The steps outlined in this test case can be used to guide the troubleshooting process.  9 
2.2.1.2.10  Supplementary test: NETCONF Access Control (Failure)  10 
This is a supplementary test to verify correct handling of NMS read attempt with incorrect privilege per 2.2.1.2.6.7. 11 
1. The NETCONF client in the NMS attempts to read user accounts provisioned on the O -RU. The NMS sends 12 
<rpc><get><filter=”subtree”> to get the configuration and operational state for the o -ran-usermgmt yang 13 
module. 14 
2. O-RU responds with <rpc-error> response with “access-denied”. 15 
Expected result is to that an O-RU will deny access to an NMS that tries to read configuration and/or operational state 16 
from models to which it does not have NACM privileges.  17 
If the test case fails, that is access is granted, vendor specific methods will be relied on to assist with troubleshooting the 18 
root cause(s) which led to the failure. 19 
2.2.2  S-Plane IOT Test 20 
This Section describes system level tests that are used to validate both S-Plane functionality and S-Plane performance 21 
between O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected using the O-RAN WG4 FH interface defined in [2] and the 22 
O-RAN WG4 M-Plane interface defined in [3].  23 
S-Plane functionality is determined by retrieval of the O-DU and O-RU synchronization state using the M-Plane or 24 
NMS as appropriate, whereas, S-Plane performance is determined by over-the-air (OTA) measurements or conductive 25 
(i.e. a cabled electrical connection to the DUT’s radio interface) measurements of O-RU synchronization signal. 26 
This Section provides a common high-level list of the items that are expected to be covered in order to validate 27 
interoperability with the relevant standard, both functional and performance aspects are addressed: 28 
• The tests apply to both 4G(LTE) and 5G(NR) and are applicable to all O-RAN IOT profiles listed in 29 
Annex A 30 
• The CUS-Plane Specification [2] Section validated is §9.3.2 31 
• SyncE Master test case is optional and only valid when the SyncE clock (eg. Implemented in the O-RU) 32 
takes advantage of it. Therefore, the related SyncE Master test cases are optional  33 
• Several test cases involve configuring the O-DU or O-RU 34 
• M-Plane connection must be established, meaning whole protocol stack ETH/IP/TCP/SSH is up and 35 
running, Capabilities are exchanged between NETCONF Client and Server, Subscriptions to notifications 36 
are created 37 
o Several test cases involve the configuration and collection of status of T-BC. However, as this is not 38 
defined in the Management Plane Specification [3], the parts of the tests below that require such 39 
functionality are FFS in this release of the specification 40 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          27 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
o Further work needs to be done to align and refine the definition of the  states in the CUS [2] and M-1 
Plane [3] specifications for the next releases 2 
The following bulleted notes apply specifically to IOT functional tests in addition to the general notes above, 3 
• Tests shall be done in the lab at constant temperature 4 
• Test equipment is needed to generate a reference S-Plane signal 5 
• For validation of synchronization information, use the FH M-Plane interface for the O-RU, and other 6 
interfaces such as NMS for O-DU  7 
• Retrieving sync-state of O-DU using the NMS is FFS in this version of the specification 8 
• O-RU reports over M-Plane the degraded received clock-class and clock-accuracy as well as locked state; 9 
details are for further study 10 
• With the exception of lls-C1, that doesn't include any T-BC in the fronthaul link, the test configuration 11 
shall use from 1 up to the maximum number of T-BCs specified for performance test, as set out in the 12 
performance test specific notes set out below, according to the preference of the tester  13 
The following bulleted notes apply specifically to IOT performance tests in addition to the general notes above, 14 
• All tests should be done in lab under constant and variable C/U plane profile. The variable C/U -Plane 15 
profile (for example similar to the test case 13 shown in figure VI.11 of ITU -T G.8261 [10]) must be 16 
defined for this test 17 
• The previous version of this document (v 1.00) contained a requirement to perform the IOT performance 18 
tests under variable temperature conditions. That requirement was removed in this version, and instead 19 
replaced with the following text that was also used in the Conformance Test specification [24]: The 20 
thermal profile is not defined. The tests are defined to be run at a constant temperature, but the thermal 21 
profile choice and range is left as a decision for the vendor 22 
• Not all cases are mandatory, a vendor or network operator may test either all or any of them 23 
• Use the maximum number of T-BC devices as shown in CUS-Plane specification [2] in Annex H  24 
Note: Annex H includes example deployment cases that capture the influence of factors including, target end-25 
to-end timing error requirement, clock type used in the network, and characteristics of the O -RU clock. 26 
Additional cases are for further study including, addressing O-RUs with different levels of clock performance, 27 
and different noise accumulation models etc 28 
• The acceptance criterion for the tests is to satisfy the 3GPP OTA TAE limits specified in 3GPP TS 36.141 29 
[18] for 4G(LTE) and 38.141-2 [19] for 5G(NR), and summarized in eCPRI [11] and ITU-T G.8271 [7]. 30 
The particular conditions applicable to each test are set out in the relevant sections below 31 
To perform the IOT S-Pane tests, following test set ups (Figure 2.5, 2.6 and 2.7) are proposed. The selection of the 32 
test setup is dependent on the configuration mode lls-C1, lls-C2, or lls-C3. This version of the document does not 33 
cover lls-C4: 34 
• Each diagram covers both functional test and conformance test of the respective synchroniz ation 35 
configuration mode. The main difference between the setups for functional and performance test is the 36 
need for a measurement equipment at the radio interface for performance test as indicated in previous 37 
paragraphs. 38 
• Each setup gives the option to select different types of S-Plane signals for the input of the O-DU. The 39 
selection of the option depends on the capability of the O-DU and operator’s synchronization architecture. 40 
In lls-C3 mode, the O-DU has the option of selecting a master through its fronthaul interface or directly 41 
connecting to a T-GM. 42 
• T-GM via a midhaul network (for ls-C1 or lls-C2) or a fronthaul network (for lls-C3) over an Ethernet 43 
interface with PTP and SyncE (if applicable) 44 
• T-GM over an Ethernet interface with PTP and SyncE (if applicable) 45

2.2.2.1 Functional test of O-DU + O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1) 1 
2.2.2.1.1  Test Description and Applicability 2 
This test validates that O-RU is synchronizing from an O-DU that incorporates a PTP grand master and SyncE Master 3 
with ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile and is traceable to a PRTC.  4 
This test involves one O-DU and one O-RU. 5 
2.2.2.1.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 6 
1. O-RU is connected to O-DU via direct fiber O-RAN links. 7 
2. The O-DU is connected to a PRTC traceable time source, directly (GNSS Receiver either embedded or 8 
connected to the O-DU) or via PTP, as described in Conformance Test Specification 2.00 [24]. 9 
2.2.2.1.3  Purpose and Scope  10 
The O-RU is synchronizing  from the O-DU with the ITU -T G.8275.1  [5] profile. This test case validates the correct 11 
synchronization status of the O-RU. 12 
2.2.2.1.4  Testability Requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU  13 
Requirements for M-Plane: must be properly operating (as defined in 2.2.1.1). 14 
Synchronization requirement: O-DU must be connected to a local or remote PRTC. 15 
2.2.2.1.5  Test Methodology 16 
These tests use the O-RAN M-Plane and O-DU NMS features. 17 
The O-DU must act as a PTP master compliant with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile. 18 
Three conditions must be covered: 19 
• startup  20 
• nominal  21 
• degraded  22 
2.2.2.1.5.1  Procedure: Startup conditions 23 
1. Not yet configured. 24 
External frequency and time source are available to the O-DU and deliver nominal status 25 
O-DU is not yet configured to select the time source and align its frequency and time to it  26 
O-DU not yet configured to act as PTP master on the FH ports 27 
2. Configured. 28 
O-DU is configured to align to the selected frequency and time source 29 
3. Until disciplining 30 
Until O-DU disciplining of the frequency and time to the selected source has completed, Startup conditions 31 
persists 32 
The O-RUs are configured to synchronize from PTP in ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile and report their status 33

G.8275.1 [5] in “nominal” status. 15

(optional) 31

• the received SyncE SSM level of the O-RU using the M-Plane (optional). Note that if SyncE state is NOK, 1

conditions, the status observation using M-plane is not available for NETCONF client. It is observed that the alarm -12 
notification is sent from the O-RU using M-Plane and the regular start-up procedures is performed. 13 
2.2.2.2 Functional test of O-DU + bridged network + O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile 14 
(LLS-C2)  15 
2.2.2.2.1  Test Description and Applicability 16 
This test validates that O-RU is synchronizing from an O-DU via a chain of T-BC using ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile.  17 
This test involves one O-DU, one O-RU and multiple T-BCs. 18 
The configuration, management, and retrieval of status of the T-BC will be considered for a future release. 19

1. O-RU is connected to O-DU via a chain of T-BCs. 21 
2. The T-BCs are class B. The subordinate port of the first T-BC is connected to O-DU. The master clock of the 22 
last T-BC is connected to the O-RU. 23 
3. The O-DU is connected to a PRTC traceable time source, directly (GNSS Receiver connected to the O-DU) or 24 
via PTP. 25 
2.2.2.2.3  Purpose and Scope  26 
The O-RU is synchronizing from the O-DU with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile over a bridged network that can deploy 27 
several T-BCs. This test case validates the correct synchronization status of the O-RU. 28 
2.2.2.2.4  Testability Requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU  29

• startup  35

• degraded  37

This test involves one O-DU, one O-RU, a PRTC/T-GM and multiple T-BCs. 33

specification.  35

2.2.2.8 Performance test of O-DU + Two O-RUs using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1) 23 
2.2.2.8.1  Test Description and applicability 24 
This test validates that the two O-RUs meet the 3GPP limits at their air interface, when  25 
• the O-DU gets its synchronization from a PRTC using either a local or remote PRTC as specified in the 26 
Conformance tests 2.00 [24], under either ideal or normal conditions ,  27 
• and is connected to two O-RUs via direct FH links,  28 
• and distributes frequency and time to these O-RUs using the ITU-T G.8275.1 (SyncE + PTP) profile 29 
2.2.2.8.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 30 
1. IOT Functional test 2.2.2.1 is successfully passed and all O-DU, bridged network elements and O-RUs report 31 
LOCKED status. 32 
2. O-RUs are connected to the O-DU via direct fiber O-RAN links. 33 
3. O-RUs are suitable for Case 1.1 or 1.2 as defined in eCPRI [11]. 34 
2.2.2.8.3  Purpose and scope 35 
The O-DU synchronize the O-RUs with the ITU-T G.8275.1 profile [5]. This test validates that the frequency and time 36 
error on the O-RU air interfaces are within the limits of the 3GPP, in both constant and variable temperature and traffic 37 
load conditions. 38 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          37 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
Only LOCKED state is tested; HOLDOVER state test is For Further Study. 1 
2.2.2.8.4 Testability Requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU  2 
Both O-DU and O-RU are running nominal software. 3 
Requirements for M-Plane: must be “up and running.” 4 
Synchronization requirement: O-DU and test equipment must be connected to a local PRTC or source traceable to 5 
PRTC. 6 
Test 2.2.2.1.6.2 is successfully passed and both O-DU and O-RUs report LOCKED status. 7 
2.2.2.8.5 Test Methodology 8 
After O-DU and O-RUs are frequency and phase locked to their PRTC synchronization source using the LLS-C1 9 
configuration, the frequency and phase errors are measured on the O-RUs air interface using a test equipment 10 
referenced to the same PRTC. 11 
The O-DU input time error on the O-DU is as specified in the Conformance Test 2.00 [24],  12 
- Either “ideal” with zero value 13 
- Or “normal”, with configured values with standard masks 14 
2.2.2.8.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  15 
For both constant and variable conditions tests, the acceptance criterion is to measure with the test equipment: 16 
• ±50 ppb maximum frequency error at the air interface 17 
• ITU-T Level 4, eCPRI Cat C (mandatory): ± 1500ns maximum absolute time error at the O-RU air 18 
interface. 19 
• ITU-T Level 6A, eCPRI Cat B (optional): ± 260ns maximum relative time error between the two O-RUs 20 
air interfaces. 21 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes an O-RU implementation suitable for Case 1.1 and case 1.2 as 22 
defined in eCPRI [11]. 23 
• ITU-T Level 6B, eCPRI Cat A (optional) ± 130ns maximum relative time error between the two O -RUs 24 
air interfaces. 25 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes an O-RU implementation suitable for Case 1.2 as defined in eCPRI 26 
[11]. It also assumes co-location of the O-RUs and O-DU. 27 
2.2.2.9 Performance test of O-DU + bridged network + Two O-RUs using ITU-T G.8275.1 28 
profile (LLS-C2)  29 
2.2.2.9.1  Test Description and applicability 30 
This test validates that the two O-RUs are meeting the 3GPP limits at their air interface, when: 31 
• the O-DU gets its synchronization from a PRTC using a local or remote PRTC as specified in the 32 
Conformance tests 2.00 [24], under either ideal or normal conditions,  33 
• and is connected to two O-RUs via eCPRI FH links via bridged network elements acting as class B T-BCs,  34 
• and distributes frequency and time to these O-RUs using the ITU-T G.8275.1 (SyncE + PTP) profile [5] 35 
2.2.2.9.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 36 
1. IOT Functional Test 2.2.2.2 is successfully passed and all O-DU, bridged network elements and O-RUs report 37 
LOCKED status. 38 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          38 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
2. O-RUs are connected to O-DU via bridged network elements acting as ITU-T G.8275.1 class B T-BCs using 1 
O-RAN links [5]. 2 
3. O-RUs are suitable for Case 1.1 or 1.2 as defined in eCPRI [11]. 3 
2.2.3.2.3  Purpose and Scope 4 
The O-DU synchronizes the O-RUs with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile via the bridged network elements. 5 
This test validates that the frequency and time error on the O-RU air interfaces are within the limits of the 3GPP, in both 6 
constant and variable temperature and traffic load conditions. 7 
Only LOCKED state is tested; HOLDOVER state test is For Further Study. 8 
2.2.2.9.4 Testability Requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU  9 
Both O-DU and O-RU are running nominal software. 10 
Requirements for M-Plane: must be “up and running” 11 
Synchronization requirement: O-DU and test equipment must be connected to a local PRTC or source traceable to 12 
PRTC. 13 
Test 2.2.2.2.6.2 is successfully passed and both O-DU and O-RUs report LOCKED status. 14 
2.2.2.9.5 Test Methodology 15 
After O-DU and O-RUs are frequency and phase locked to their PRTC synchronization source using the LLS-C2 16 
configuration, the frequency and phase errors are measured on the O -RUs air interface using a test equipment 17 
referenced to the same PRTC. 18 
The O-DU input time error on the O-DU is as specified in the Conformance Test 2.00 [24],  19 
- Either “ideal” with zero value 20 
- Or “normal”, with configured values with standard masks. 21 
2.2.2.9.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  22 
For both constant and variable conditions tests, the acceptance criterion is to measure with the test equipment: 23 
• ±50 ppb maximum frequency error 24 
• ITU-T Level 4, eCPRI Cat C (mandatory): ± 1500ns maximum absolute time error at the O-RU air 25 
interface. 26 
• ITU-T Level 6A, eCPRI Cat B (optional): ± 260ns maximum relative time error between the two O -RUs 27 
air interfaces. 28 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes up to 1 (respectively 2) class B T-BC on the path between the 29 
branching one and each O-RU implementation suitable for case 1.1 (respectively case 1.2) as defined in 30 
eCPRI [11]. 31 
• ITU-T Level 6B, eCPRI Cat A (optional) ± 130ns maximum relative time error between the two O-RUs 32 
air interfaces. 33 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes direct fiber link between the branching class B T -BC and each O-RU 34 
implementation suitable case 1.2 as defined in eCPRI [11] (not supported by case 1.1). It also assumes co-35 
location of the O-RUs and O-DU. 36

2.2.2.10 Performance test of O-DU + bridged network + Two O-RUs using ITU-T 1 
G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C3) 2 
2.2.2.10.1  Test Description and applicability 3 
This test validates that the two O-RUs are meeting the 3GPP limits at their air interface, and the O-DU is meeting time 4 
error limits defined in CUS-Plane specification [2] when 5 
• both O-DU and O-RUs get their synchronization from a PRTC using SyncE + PTP over a Full Timing 6 
Support network (ITU-T G.8275.1 profile [5], ITU-T G.8271.1 network limits [7]) 7 
2.2.2.10.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 8 
1. IOT Functional Test 2.2.2.3 is successfully passed and all O-DU, bridged network elements and O-RUs report 9 
LOCKED status. 10 
2. O-RUs and O-DU are connected to bridged network elements acting as ITU-T G.8275.1 class B T-BCs using 11 
O-RAN links [5]. This FH network has a local PRTC distributing SyncE and PTP to both O-DU and O-RUs. 12 
3. O-RUs are suitable for Case 1.1 or 1.2 as defined in eCPRI [11]. 13 
2.2.2.10.3  Purpose and scope 14 
The FH network synchronizes all O-DU and O-RUs with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile via the bridged network 15 
elements. 16 
This test validates that the frequency and time error on the O-RU air interfaces and O-DU are within the limits of the 17 
3GPP, in both constant and variable temperature and traffic load conditions. 18 
Only LOCKED state is tested; HOLDOVER state test is For Further Study. 19 
2.2.2.10.4 Testability Requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU  20 
Both O-DU and O-RU are running nominal software. 21 
Requirements for M-Plane: must be “up and running” 22 
Synchronization requirement: FH network and test equipment must be connected to a local PRTC or source traceable to 23 
PRTC. 24 
Test 2.2.2.3.6.2 is successfully passed and both O-DU and O-RUs report LOCKED status. 25 
2.2.2.10.5 Test Methodology 26 
After O-DU and O-RUs are frequency and phase locked to their PRTC synchronization source using the LLS-C3 27 
configuration, the frequency and phase errors are measured at the O-RUs air interface using a test equipment referenced 28 
to the same PRTC. 29 
The PRTC output time error on the O-DU is as specified in the Conformance Test 2.00 [24],  30 
- Either “ideal” with zero value 31 
- Or “normal”, with configured values with standard masks. 32 
2.2.2.10.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  33 
For both constant and variable conditions tests, the acceptance criterion is to measure with the test equipment: 34 
• ±50 ppb maximum frequency error (mandatory): at the O-RU air interface 35 
• ITU-T Level 4, eCPRI Cat C (mandatory): ± 1500ns maximum absolute time error at the O-RU air 36 
interface and at the O-DU output test signal (for example 1PPS). 37

• ITU-T Level 6A, eCPRI Cat B (optional): ± 260ns maximum relative time error between the two O -RUs 1 
air interfaces. 2 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes up to 1 (respectively 2) class B T-BC on the path between the 3 
branching one and each O-RU implementation suitable for case 1.1 (respectively case 1.2) as defined in 4 
eCPRI [11]. 5 
• ITU-T Level 6B, eCPRI Cat A (optional) ± 130ns maximum relative time error between the two O -RUs 6 
air interfaces. 7 
Note: This level of accuracy assumes direct fiber link between the branching class B T -BC and each O-RU 8 
implementation suitable case 1.2 as defined in eCPRI [11] (not supported by case 1.1). It also assumes co-9 
location of the O-RUs and O-DU. 10

2.2.3  C/U-Plane IOT Test 21 
2.2.3.1  Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment and Initial Radio U-Plane data transfer 22 
2.2.3.1.1  Test Description and Applicability 23 
This is a Radio system level test which is used to validate the radio system functionalities, performance and multi-24 
vendor interoperability of the O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected using the O-RAN WG4 specified FH 25 
interface [2], [3].  26 
This test validates if a UE can perform Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment and initial Radio U-Plane data transfer 27 
procedures with the network which includes the O-DU and O-RU as an integrated system under test in this test setup. 28 
Although there is no FH focused testing for C/U-Plane in this test, it is still possible to observe successful 29 
interoperability via positive test outcomes for this test. ie, if radio system level test passes, it can be assumed that O-30 
RAN WG4 specified FH interface C/U-Plane is successfully working. 31 
This scenario is MANDATORY. 32 
The DUTs are a single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)) and a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU)). 33 
This test shall be executed using whichever IOT profile(s) are appropriate for the DUTs.  See Annex A for details on the 34 
IOT profiles. 35 
2.2.3.1.2  Minimum Requirements (Prerequisites) 36 
Single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)) and a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU))  37 
• Must be connected through the O-RAN FH  38

• Must be synchronized with the common S-Plane configuration 1

the 3GPP 5G F1 interface with the O-DU(s) (DUT) 7

mode  9

mode 11

mode 13

C/U-Plane procedural flows and contents 19

2.2.3.1.3  Test Purpose and Scope 23 
Purpose of this test is to validate key radio operation after M-Plane startup, ie, Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment and 24 
initial Radio U-Plane data transfer on system level with integration of O-DU and O-RU from different vendors. 25 
Note that this test requires both Downlink and Uplink Radio Layer 3 C-Plane message. This means that this test also 26 
validates both transfer of Downlink and Uplink FH U-Plane message and related Downlink FH C-Plane messages. 27 
2.2.3.1.4  Testability requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU 28 
Nominal software runs on the O-RU and O-DU. 29 
2.2.3.1.5  Test Methodology 30 
2.2.3.1.5.1  Initial Conditions 31 
1. O-RU and O-DU are both in service, ie, M-Plane start-up procedure is completed, and broadcast channels are 32 
being transmitted  33 
2. Test UE or UE emulator has not yet been registered with the network 34 
2.2.3.1.5.2  Procedure: Nominal test 35 
Performs Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure using the Test UE or UE emulator. Note that R adio Layer 3 36 
C-Plane establishment procedure depends on the 5G NR operation mode. In the case when the DUTs are operating in 37 
NSA mode, Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure includes Attach procedure and/or service request procedure 38 
specified in 3GPP TS 23.401 [20] and EN-DC setup procedure specified in 3GPP TS 37.340 [22]. In the case when the 39 
DUTs are operating in SA mode, Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure includes Registration procedure and 40 
service request procedure specified in 3GPP TS 23.502 [21].  41

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          42 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
Performs data transfer from the application test server to the Test UE or UE emulator. The application test server 1 
generates and transmits 10 IP packets with each packet 32 bytes in size. 2 
Note that data transfer depends on the operation mode. In the case when the DUTs are operating in NSA mode, data 3 
transfers can be performed over Default EPS bearer using SN terminated split bearer specified in 3GPP TS 37.340 [22]. 4 
In case when the DUTs are operating in SA mode, data transfers can be performed over PDU Session and QoS flow 5 
specified in 3GPP TS 23.502 [21].  6 
This test case does not specify the test data pattern generated by the application test server, but it is recommended that 7 
the test data pattern should include some level of randomness (ie, avoiding all zeros). 8 
2.2.3.1.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  9 
Observe the Test UE or emulated UE can perform Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment successfully and can perform 10 
data transfers over the network particularly through the O-DU and O-RU. 11 
Record Test UE or UE emulator logs that the Radio Layer 3 (eg. RRC/NAS) message flows are per 3GPP TS 23.401 12 
[20] Sections 5.3.4, 5.4 and 3GPP TS 37.340 [22] in NSA mode and 3GPP TS 23.502 [21] Sections 4.2.3, 4.3 in SA 13 
mode.  14 
Record Test UE or UE emulator Radio U-Plane logs that the data packets transferred by application test server (ie, 10 IP 15 
packets of 32 bytes) are received correctly. 16

2.2.3.2.5  Test Methodology 18 
2.2.3.2.5.1 Initial Conditions 19 
1. O-RU and O-DU are both in service, ie, M-Plane start-up procedure has been completed and broadcast 20 
channels are being transmitted. 21 
2. Test UE or UE emulator has registered to the network, ie, Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure is 22 
completed. Note that Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure depends on operation mode. In case 23 
when the of DUTs are operating in NSA mode, Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure includes 24

procedure specified in 3GPP TS 37.340 [22]. In case when the of DUTs are operating in SA mode, Radio 26 
Layer 3 C-Plane establishment procedure includes means Registration procedure and service request procedure 27 
specified in 3GPP TS 23.502 [21]. 28 
2.2.3.2.5.2  Procedure: Nominal test 29 
Performs downlink data transfer from application test server to the Test UE or UE emulator. The application test server 30 
generates and transmits downlink data with data size large enough to achieve the maximum Layer 1 Radio data rate, 31 
which is specified in 2.2.4.2.6, for the duration of the test. The duration of the test is 20 seconds.  32 
Note that data transfer depends on the operation mode. In case when the DUTs are operating in NSA mode, data 33 
transfers can be performed over Default EPS bearer using SN terminated split bearer specified in 3GPP TS 37.340 [22]. 34 
In case when the DUTs are operating in SA mode, data transfers can be performed over PDU Session and QoS flow 35 
specified in 3GPP TS 23.502 [21].  36 
This test case does not specify the test data pattern generated by the application test server, but it is recommended that 37 
the test data pattern should include some level of randomness (ie, avoiding all zeros). 38 
2.2.3.2.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  39 
Observe that the Test UE or emulated UE can perform Radio U-Plane data transfers over the network particularly 40 
through the O-DU and O-RU at the target data rate. 41 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          44 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
Record the Test UE or UE emulator Radio U-Plane logs and determine that they contain measurements such as the 1 
measured Radio U-Plane data rates during the test. The acceptance criterion is that Radio U-Plane data rate on average 2 
during the test duration achieves the performance level defined as follows 3 
Performance level 4 
Target data rate = Maximum Layer 1 Radio data rate * (1 - Ratio of Radio resource overhead) * Margin,  5 
where 6 
Maximum Layer 1 Radio data rate is calculated based on 3GPP TS 38. 211 [15] and TS 38.214 [23] by using RAN 7 
parameters, ie, Total channel bandwidth, TDD configuration (when TDD), number of spatial/antenna streams, 8 
modulation order and coding rate. Note that these RAN parameters are defined in the IOT profiles (see Annex A for 9 
details).  10 
Ratio of Radio resource overhead is calculated based on 3GPP TS 38.211 [15] by using Radio physical layer 11 
channel configurations, eg, PDCCH resource mapping, Reference signal resource mapping, and so on, assumed in 12 
the IOT setup. Note that the physical layer channel configurations are part of the radio test setup configuration. 13 
Margin is assumed in order to account for issues other than the FH. The value of Margin is 0.8. 14
