2.2.4  C/U-Plane Delay Management IOT Test 15 
The test cases defined in this section will validate that the transmitted Control - and User-data packets sent from the O-16 
DU are received within the reception windows at the O-RU by checking that the frame timing on the air interface is 17 
correct. 18 
The same is applicable for uplink direction, i.e. that the User-data packets sent from the O-RU are received within the 19 
reception window on the O-DU, this is done by checking that it is possible for a test UE to attach and send data. 20 
For all currently defined IOT Profiles the O-DU timing advance type is ‘Fixed Timing Advance’. The Figure below is 21 
copied from the CUS-Specification section 2.3.5 “Latency Categories for O-DU with fixed timing advance”. 22 
 23 
Figure 2-8: CUS-Specification section 2.3.5 “Latency Categories for O-DU with fixed timing advance”. 24 
The Figure shows the downlink timing when fixed timing is used, the point TXDL_Start is a fixed point in relation to the 25 
“OTA transmission” point. 26 
The O-DU needs only to be configured with T12max, T12min and Tcp_adv_dl the values are taken from the profile that is used 27 
when running these test cases. The Tcp_adv_dl value is the time in advance the O-RU needs the C-Plane messages before 28 
the U-Plane information is received by the O-RU. These test cases assume a symmetric latency in the Fronthaul 29 
Network, i.e. T12=T34. 30 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          47 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
These test cases assume that the difference between “fixed timing advance” and “dynamic timing advance” is that for 1 
“fixed timing advance” the O-DU will advance the transmission of downlink data the same amount of  time for all 2 
connected O-RUs regardless of the individual fronthaul latency, for “dynamic timing advance” the advancement could 3 
be different per O-RU and thus e.g. T12max must be configured per O-RU. 4 
An O-DU running in “Fixed Timing Advance”-mode is an O-DU that has the ability to handle a specific value for T1a 5 
(sum of fronthaul latency T12 and O-RU processing delay T2a). The O-DU will set the TXDL_Start to this fixed value 6 
independent on actual T12_max value. 7 
TXmaxlls-CU will vary due to different line-rates of the fronthaul interface and amount of data (control+user) that is sent 8 
for a specific symbol. 9 
2.2.4.1  Test environment 10 
Testing tools which are required for the delay management test cases. 11 
• Single Test UE or UE emulator: used to perform Radio Layer 3 C-Plane establishment and Radio U-Plane 12 
data transfers with the network 13 
• O-CU or O-CU emulator either as a separate node or as a combined node with the O -DU(s) (DUT): used 14 
to provide Layer 2 and Layer 3 radio processing on the network side. In case of se parate node, terminates 15 
the 3GPP 5G F1 interface with the O-DU(s) (DUT) 16 
• 4G Core network or 4G Core network emulator: used to terminate UEs (emulator) NAS protocol in NSA 17 
mode 18 
• 4G MeNB or 4G MeNB emulator: used to terminate the 3GPP EN-DC X2 interface with 5G CU in NSA 19 
mode 20 
• 5G Core Network or 5G Core Network emulator: used to terminate UEs (emulator) NAS protocol in SA 21 
mode 22 
• Application test server: used to generate and terminate application layer traffic (eg. UDP, TWAMP, etc) 23 
and provide application layer processing on the network side. 24 
Testing tools which can be useful for this test scenario particularly for validating that the DUTs are configured and 25 
operating correctly during the test, troubleshooting and detailed validation purposes  26 
• FH Protocol Analyzer: used for protocol analysis of O-RAN FH protocols in this specific test scenario, 27 
C/U-Plane procedural flows and contents 28 
• RF Spectrum and Beam Signal Analyzer: used for RF and Beam power and quality analysis ensuring that 29 
the O-RU (DUT1(O-RU)) is transmitting correctly on the configured broadcast and synchronization 30 
signals on the downlink 31 
  32

Figure 2-9: Delay-management test environment 1 
2.2.4.2  Timing accuracy definition 2 
When in “Test Requirement (expected result)” it is stated “… timing accuracy at the antenna reference point is 3 
according to requirement” the following is applicable. 4 
In ORAN WG4 CUS-specification section 9.2.5.4 “Air interface maximum time error”, tables 9 -1 and 9-2 lists the 5 
3GPP air interface timing accuracy for different LTE and 5G features. The timing accuracy requirements are divided 6 
into 2 alternatives, relative or absolute time errors. 7 
Depending on what 3GPP features that are to be supported by a specific IOT-profile different timing accuracy 8 
requirement is thus applicable. 9 
2.2.4.3  Delay Management #1, minimum fronthaul latency 10 
2.2.4.3.1  Test Description and Applicability 11 
This is a Radio system level test which is used to validate the radio system functionalities, performance and multi-12 
vendor interoperability of the O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected using the O-RAN WG4 specified FH 13 
interface [2], [3]. 14 
This test validates that the O-RU will transmit the user data at correct point in time and with correct content during 15 
different conditions related to the fronthaul interface latency between the O -DU and the O-RU. 16 
2.2.4.3.2  Minimum Requirements 17 
Single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)) and a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU)) 18 
• Must be connected through the O-RAN FH 19 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          49 
                                                                                         O-RAN.WG4.IOT.0-v04.00 
• Must be synchronized with the common S-Plane configuration 1 
2.2.4.3.3  Test Purpose 2 
Purpose of this test is to validate that correct timing is achieved on the air interface regardless of the actual fronthaul 3 
latency and O-RU processing time. 4 
2.2.4.3.4  Testability requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU 5 
Nominal software runs on the O-RU and O-DU. 6 
2.2.4.3.5  Test Methodology 7 
2.2.4.3.5.1  Initial Conditions 8 
1. The fronthaul latency should be at a minimum for this test case. The T12_min in current IOT-Profiles is 0µs. 9 
0µs is not possible to achieve in reality, instead the shortest possible fronthaul latency with existing test 10 
equipment is sufficient for this initial condition. 11 
2. O-RU and O-DU are both in service, i.e. M-Plane start-up procedure is completed and broadcast channels are 12 
being transmitted  13 
3. Test UE or UE emulator has registered to the network, i.e. Radio Layer 3 C -Plane establishment procedure is 14 
completed. 15 
2.2.4.3.5.2  Procedure: Nominal test 16 
Performs downlink and uplink data transfer to/from the test UE. 17 
2.2.4.3.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  18 
Observe that: 19 
1. With Fronthaul Protocol Analyzer (connected at the O-DU-end of fronthaul interface), observe that the 20 
fronthaul C- and U-Plane messages transmitted by the O-DU are transmitted within respective plane’s 21 
transmission windows. 22 
2. With Fronthaul Protocol Analyzer (connected at the O-RU-end of fronthaul interface), observe that the 23 
fronthaul C- and U-Plane messages in downlink direction are received within respective plane’s reception 24 
window by the O-RU.  25 
3. With the RF Spectrum Analyzer, observe that the air interface transmission timing accuracy at the antenna 26 
reference point is according to requirements as specified in section 2.2. 4.2. Also observe that frame numbering, 27 
slot and symbol timing is according to section 9.7.2 “System Frame Number Calculation from GPS Time” in 28 
CUS-Specification. 29 
4. With Fronthaul Protocol Analyzer (connected at the O-RU-end of fronthaul interface), observe that the U-Plane 30 
messages transmitted by the O-RU (uplink direction) are transmitted within the O-RU’s transmission window. 31 
2.2.4.4  Delay Management #2, maximum fronthaul latency 32 
2.2.4.4.1  Test Description and Applicability 33 
This is a Radio system level test which is used to validate the radio system functionalities, performance and multi-34 
vendor interoperability of the O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected using the O-RAN WG4 specified FH 35 
interface [2], [3]. 36 
This test validates that the O-RU will transmit the user data at correct point in time and with correct content during 37 
different conditions related to the fronthaul interface between the O-DU and the O-RU. 38

2.2.4.6  Delay Management #4, larger fronthaul latency then supported 1 
2.2.4.6.1  Test Description and Applicability 2 
This is a Radio system level test which is used to validate the radio system functionalities, performance and multi-3 
vendor interoperability of the O-DU and O-RU from different vendors connected using the O-RAN WG4 specified FH 4 
interface [2], [3]. 5 
This test validates that the O-RU will not transmit anything on the air interface when the latency in the fronthaul 6 
network is larger than is supported by the O-RU, i.e. the C- and U-Plane messages will be received too late on the O-7 
RU (outside its reception window) and thus be dropped by the O-RU. 8 
2.2.4.6.2  Minimum Requirements 9 
Single O-DU (DUT1(O-DU)) and a single O-RU (DUT1(O-RU)) 10 
• Must be connected through the O-RAN FH 11 
• Must be synchronized with the common S-Plane configuration 12 
2.2.4.6.3  Test Purpose 13 
Purpose of this test is to validate that correct timing is achieved on the air interface regardless of the actual fronthaul 14 
latency and O-RU processing time. 15 
2.2.4.6.4  Testability requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU 16 
Nominal software runs on the O-RU and O-DU. 17 
2.2.4.6.5  Test Methodology 18 
2.2.4.6.5.1  Initial Conditions 19 
1. The fronthaul latency should be set to a value that is larger than the O-DU’s category specifies. 20 
2.2.4.6.5.2  Procedure: Nominal test 21 
- 22 
2.2.4.6.6  Test Requirement (expected result)  23 
Observe that the no cell is being transmitted by the O-RU over the air interface.24

name and the particular version of the WG4 IOT specification to ensure that the appropria te set of profile parameters are referenced. Where such change has occurred from one 4 
release to the next the change is called out with a footnote. 5
